  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12284663032906329738">What happened 500 years ago was never supposed to resurface.<br/>Exploring his Grandma’s scary manor, Archibald stumbles upon a dark family secret, linked to a time of great fears and superstitions. Key to that mystery: an ancient terrestrial globe, populated by the most fantastic creatures.<br/>When he unlocks the storm inside by accident, the risk-averse boy gets whisked into the </span>
  <span id="freeText12284663032906329738" style="display:none">What happened 500 years ago was never supposed to resurface.<br />Exploring his Grandma’s scary manor, Archibald stumbles upon a dark family secret, linked to a time of great fears and superstitions. Key to that mystery: an ancient terrestrial globe, populated by the most fantastic creatures.<br />When he unlocks the storm inside by accident, the risk-averse boy gets whisked into the underworld of Lemurea, where a battle started in the Middle Ages has yet to be settled. Down here, it’s light versus darkness, magic versus fire, witches versus dragons. But not any kind of witches —an army of young girls, with the most magical weapons. And not any kind of dragons —Marodors, enigmatic monsters, part beast, part human, which will make you rethink everything you thought you knew about dragons.<br />While Archibald is thrust into an amazing adventure that will test his survival skills, on the flip side of the Earth, his sister Hailee faces her own challenges. Seeking to solve Archibald’s disappearance, she uncovers the grim plans of a dark priest.<br />Two breathtaking stories, running parallel with one another, but tightly intertwined. Two worlds, on a dangerous collision course...<br />---<br />The first installment in a phenomenal series, The Lost Witches reads like an addicting thriller —and sets the stage for more adventures to come for Archibald Finch.</span>

<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589734946i/29494799._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>If you've ever wondered which literary world would be the best to live in, wonder no longer, cause there's a <b><u><a href='https://youtu.be/SREpUj0py9o' rel='nofollow noopener'>BookTube Video</a></u></b> to answer that!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b>:<blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579317815i/28797187._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>It's the calm before the storm. Or perhaps simply a lull before the next one.</i>
</blockquote>Archibald Finch and his family (mom, dad and older sister (Hailee)) just moved into his <b>Grandma's scary old manor. </b><br/><br/>Archibald spends the first few days exploring...and stumbles upon<b> a mysterious globe. </b><br/><br/>It has weird and strange illustrations of cre</span>
  <span id="freeText8601346454178146903" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589734946i/29494799._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>If you've ever wondered which literary world would be the best to live in, wonder no longer, cause there's a <b><u><a href="https://youtu.be/SREpUj0py9o" rel="nofollow noopener">BookTube Video</a></u></b> to answer that!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b>:<blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579317815i/28797187._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>It's the calm before the storm. Or perhaps simply a lull before the next one.</i>
</blockquote>Archibald Finch and his family (mom, dad and older sister (Hailee)) just moved into his <b>Grandma's scary old manor. </b><br><br>Archibald spends the first few days exploring...and stumbles upon<b> a mysterious globe. </b><br><br>It has weird and strange illustrations of creepy and impossible creatures...and when he touches it just right, it emitted a bright light and suddenly he was <b>sucked into an entirely new world.</b><blockquote>
  <i>"What a freaky place!"</i>
</blockquote>This new place is full of warrior women - well...girls - who've been stuck there for <b>nearly five hundred years.</b><blockquote>
  <i>"Is that why they sent you here?" asks Archibald. "To save you?"</i>
</blockquote>And...it's infested with Marodors - demonic entities - each with far too many limbs or teeth...and an unyielding hunger for anything that walks by.<br><br>Archibald is going to have to learn how to adapt - and fast - before<b> he turns into someone's lunch.</b><br><br>Meanwhile Hailee, his sister, is stuck in the real world...and <b>no one believes what she saw. </b>She's desperate to find Archibald and get him out of the globe.<br><br>But when she asks the wrong person, she gets far more trouble than she bargained for. <br><br>She's going to have to keep herself one step ahead of them to stay alive...<b>and time is ticking.</b><br><br>The story - 4.5 stars... the story with the gorgeous illustrations -<b>
  <i> a million stars.</i>
</b><br><br>This one ended up being SO much fun and I'm so happy to have gotten to read it.<br><br>I loved the creativity seen in the world-building. I was wholly enamored with the world that Archibald falls into (though, this does NOT mean I want to follow him there. I'm perfectly happy reading about the Marodors from my safe and comfy bed). <br><br>I also really liked the <b>sheer uniqueness of the monsters</b> in this book - it made for a very varied adventure (and now I'm incredibly curious what their Marodor guidebook would look like!).<br><br>I started off slightly disliking Archibald - he seemed a bit like a know-it-all and I just couldn't pinpoint his character. But as the story grew and developed, I really started to like him and he really came into his personality.<br><br>Hailee - Archibald's sister - was probably <b>my favorite character.</b> Her down-to-earth attitude was really well-done and believable.<br><br>Also, I would be doing this book a complete disservice if I didn't mention the absolutely <b>GORGEOUS </b>illustrations.<br><br>Seriously - every chapter had <b>stunning black-and-white art</b> that completely drew me into this story and really bumped it up a notch. <br><br>The illustrator is so incredibly talented and I really think the author made the right decision by bringing her on board. <br><br>I am keeping my fingers crossed that the next book will also feature her amazing artwork.<br><br>All in all, I absolutely adored this book and<b> cannot recommend this middle grade book enough!</b><br><br><i>A huge thank you to the author for sending me a free copy in exchange for an honest review</i><br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2614876789" />
    <a title="Whispering Stories" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20354973-whispering-stories"><img alt="Whispering Stories" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548065529p2/20354973.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2614876789?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whispering Stories" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whispering Stories" href="/user/show/20354973-whispering-stories">Whispering Stories</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2614876789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3578692788319786095">Book Reviewed by Stacey on <a href='https://www.whisperingstories.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>www.whisperingstories.com</a><br/><br/>When Archibald’s Grandmother dies the family including his parents and his sister move into her huge mansion, complete with Manservant. Whilst on the hunt for his Christmas present, which his mother tells him she hasn’t bought, he discovers a box hidden on a shelf in the library and mistakes it for his gift.<br/><br/>Inside is an old globe with countries on he doesn’t recognise. He has a feeling that the globe opens somehow and fiddles with it to try to </span>
  <span id="freeText3578692788319786095" style="display:none">Book Reviewed by Stacey on <a href="https://www.whisperingstories.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.whisperingstories.com</a><br /><br />When Archibald’s Grandmother dies the family including his parents and his sister move into her huge mansion, complete with Manservant. Whilst on the hunt for his Christmas present, which his mother tells him she hasn’t bought, he discovers a box hidden on a shelf in the library and mistakes it for his gift.<br /><br />Inside is an old globe with countries on he doesn’t recognise. He has a feeling that the globe opens somehow and fiddles with it to try to see inside. Unfortunately, the globe is more than it seems, it is like a key to another world and sucks Archibald and half his bedroom furniture inside to an old, magical world called Lemurea where female witches live together and fight the evil beasts that occupy this world. Their only protection is the Golem stones.<br /><br />Whilst Archibald is in the magical world, his sister Hailee is in the present day searching for her brother and trying to find out about the globe, not realising someone who has been looking for it a long time is on her tail. What the siblings don’t understand is how entwined the two worlds are.<br /><br />Archibald and the Lost Witches is the first book in a planned series by Michel Guyon. It is a fascinating adventure with mythical beasts, evil beings, and a magical world, plus some feisty witches with attitudes. The chapters have perfect titles and there are the most amazing illustrations throughout too.<br /><br />We get to spend time in Lemurea with Archibald and London with Hailee and it was nice to have the two storylines co-existing and delve in deeper into the plot with both brother and sister who have very different personalities. Archibald is a bit of a geek and a know-it-all. He absorbs information easily. Whereas Hailee is more your average teenager who gets annoyed easily by her little brother but you realise how much she must love him to never stop searching for him.<br /><br />There are a lot of MG books that incorporate magical, mystery worlds, witches, and beasts but I feel this book stands on its own merits. It is not like any other MG book I have read.<br /><br />The book is exciting and absorbing the whole way through and you never know what is coming next, keeping you on your toes and pleasantly surprised throughout. My only concern for the book is how many pages the book has for an MG book. I do hope this doesn’t put anyone off reading it as the book is completely mesmerising from beginning to end and really is worth your time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3578692788319786095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2532323358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2532323358" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Sagan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53505099-elizabeth-sagan"><img alt="Elizabeth Sagan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527068343p2/53505099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2532323358?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Sagan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Sagan" href="/user/show/53505099-elizabeth-sagan">Elizabeth Sagan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2532323358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13819828669590723131">I’m not a fan of middle grade books, but...<br/>BUT.<br/>This book.<br/>THIS BOOK.<br/>This book is the book that you’re reading when you're 13 years old, on a cold winter day/evening/night, with a cup of hot tea/chocolate/milk. This book is the definition of cozy and childhood. It has everything a middle grade book should have. I’m going to quickly mention the amazing illustrations, the wonderful way they are put together, how the text goes around them, the high quality hardcover and dust jacket. Now to the story,</span>
  <span id="freeText13819828669590723131" style="display:none">I’m not a fan of middle grade books, but...<br />BUT.<br />This book.<br />THIS BOOK.<br />This book is the book that you’re reading when you're 13 years old, on a cold winter day/evening/night, with a cup of hot tea/chocolate/milk. This book is the definition of cozy and childhood. It has everything a middle grade book should have. I’m going to quickly mention the amazing illustrations, the wonderful way they are put together, how the text goes around them, the high quality hardcover and dust jacket. Now to the story, characters, and writing style. I honestly can find no flaw. Maybe I wasn’t particularly fond of how Helena was built (but that’s only at the end and only because I didn’t like her as a person), but that’s the only thing that I can think about. Other than that, the story, the characters, everything is on point.<br />Something that I really, really enjoyed – the jokes. This book is full of them. And they are so funny!<br />I pondered whether I should give it 4 stars or 5 stars. The only reason why I would have given it 4 stars is because, as I mentioned, middle grade books aren’t my jam. Of course I can’t compare the feeling they are giving me with the feeling that a (good) Stephen King book gives me. But it wouldn’t be fair to take a star from a very good book only because I’m not the targeted audience. Because make no mistake – this is an amazing book. So I’ll render to Caesar the things that are Caesar’s.<br />If I’d have a kid, I’d give him Archibald to read, just as I would give him Harry Potter and Percy Jackson. Mark my words, this has the potential of becoming something big.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText2459312515317335041" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570739352i/28274869.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>This is the first illustration in the book. What an amazing library, at the heart of the old manor Archibald and family inherit following his grandma's passing, and at the heart of the story... Lots of mysteries in this room, and lots of secrets...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570139484i/28240551.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>There's something really old-fashioned and magical about the layout of this book that I really enjoyed.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570139484i/28240552.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>A kid gets drawn into the unknown... and lands in a fantasy world with part of his bedroom... my dream since I was 5!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570139126i/28240542.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>I love the cover, not just because it's pretty, but also for what it says... (a lot) and what it leaves to the imagination... (even more!)</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570139484i/28240553.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Lemurea, that's the name of the dark underworld in the book, is a pretty scary place, infested with enigmatic creatures, called Marodors, part beast, part human...</b><br><br>Right from the start, I was hooked! The premise pulled me right in. That manor Archibald's parents inherit, the mysteries he discovers little by little, that hidden world he gains access to... what a fabulous idea! And it only gets better from there. I also loved the fact that this book surprised me, several times over. The link to Da Vinci in particular is great in the sense that it sounds entirely plausible. So many secrets, so many clues, so much magic, and the author managed to wrap them all perfectly into one book, even though many questions and mysteries remain unanswered... which makes me excited about the rest fo the series.<br>I have the feeling that Archibald Finch will no doubt join the ranks of enduring great Middle Grade classics. I'm thinking Peter Pan, Narnia and Harry Potter especially. If (hopefully) turned into a movie, I'm sure this will be box-office gold. Something else to look forward to.<br>Another thing that I loved about the book is the layout and the way the texts wraps around the amazing illustrations. I think there are about 25 drawings in the book. I'm sharing a few here. Her adventure is at least as exciting as the one Archibald himself experiences. And the fact that it happens during Christmas time only makes it more magical. (And I'm not saying this because London is my city..!)</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570139484i/28240555.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The monsters in the book are some of the most complex and elaborate I've ever seen, especially this one, the Krakatorum, depicted here during an epic battle involving a weird looking tank with an incredible background... (I won't say any more to avoid spoilers!) As to what those creatures really are, it's probably the most interesting part of the book...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570139484i/28240556.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The general atmosphere is all about mystery, old myths and ancient legends. It doesn't matter if you're in Lemurea or London, the magic is everywhere. And again, superb layout.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570139484i/28240557.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>I recommend the hardcover for this book. Look at this dust jacket. It's just stunning!!!</b></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2959837630">

<div id="review_2580572493" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2580572493" />
    <a title="Ivy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5894971-ivy"><img alt="Ivy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548574807p2/5894971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2580572493?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivy" href="/user/show/5894971-ivy">Ivy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5894971-ivy?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5894971-ivy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5894971-ivy?shelf=about-magic">about-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5894971-ivy?shelf=top-reads-in-2019">top-reads-in-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2580572493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15695914118270991499">When Michel Guyen asked me if I wanted to read and review his book I was thrilled. The book sounded amazing; adventuoures and full of magic. I love middle grade books; especially when I want to escape everyday life I usually pick up a middle grade book as I love how they remind me of my own childhood; when I spent days and nights reading. There’s just something nostalgic about it. Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches is definitely one of those books that bring out the hidden child in us. It’s a </span>
  <span id="freeText15695914118270991499" style="display:none">When Michel Guyen asked me if I wanted to read and review his book I was thrilled. The book sounded amazing; adventuoures and full of magic. I love middle grade books; especially when I want to escape everyday life I usually pick up a middle grade book as I love how they remind me of my own childhood; when I spent days and nights reading. There’s just something nostalgic about it. Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches is definitely one of those books that bring out the hidden child in us. It’s a book you want to read on a cold winter night, cuddled up in a warm blanket with a hot chocolate. <br /><br />This book has everything a good middle grade book should have. It has not only one hero, but several; heroes who are completely different from most. This book is a huge adventure, perfect for daydreamers and little adventurers. There are lots of unique, magical and mystical elements to discover. There is a thousand year old secret, dusty antique shops, a mysterious globe, an old mansion – all this and so much more. It’s about witches, but not just any witches, and it’s about dragons, that are so different to how we usually imagine them to be. The enigmatic, giant and deadly creatures are called Marodors and they are half human, half monsters. Also Family plays a huge and important part in this book, which is usually rarely the case in fantasy novels. Another thing that I really absolutely enjoyed was the jokes. This book is so funny, it’s wonderful. <br /><br />The characters are incredible lovable and charismatic; they are all odd in their own way, sometimes a little bit naïve but so wonderfully written that it’s really hard to choose a favorite. <br /><br />There’s so much magic in this book; as soon as you start reading you will feel like you’re part of this adventure. This book does not only entertain, but also inspire and enchant. <br /><br />The story is told from two different points of view: Archibald, who tries to survive in a mysterious land called Lemurea and his older sister Hailee, who stayed behind in London and tries to find her missing brother, who has vanished in front of her eyes. I can’t even say which perspective I liked better, the one in Lemurea with all the magical and scary creatures, the witches and the fights, or the one in London, which is basically an exciting and dangerous scavenger hunt through the city. <br /><br />Lemurea is a great, but still mostly unexplored world that holds so many secrets and dangers. It needs some more depth and room for all the characters to grow and the world to expand but this is only the beginning of it; the beginning of something big and I am sure the next book will have a lot more in store for us. <br /><br />I’m also going to quickly mention the beautiful illustrations, which give the book that little bit of extra. They give you an even clearer idea of the world that Michel Guyen created. The drawings are really gorgeous and partly really scary but they are put together in such a nice way. <br /><br />Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches is the perfect coming of age story. It is action packed, enigmatic, adventurous and simply magical. Archibald Finch won over my heart quickly. I enjoyed every single page of the story and I can’t even put into words how excited I am to read the next book, which I hope will be published soon. If you also have a weak spot for middle grade books, fantasy or just stories with great charming, slightly weird characters, then this book is just the perfect read for you. I’d definitely recommend you to pick it up as soon as possible. This book series has the potential to become something BIG and I very much hope that one day the children in this world will mention the name Archibald Finch in the same breath as Harry Potter and Percy Jackson. <br /><br />Thank you so much Michel Guyen, for sending me a review copy of your book. I absolutely loved it. Can’t wait for the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15695914118270991499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2576697481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2576697481" />
    <a title="Charlotte P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88623584-charlotte-p"><img alt="Charlotte P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540795713p2/88623584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2576697481?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte P." href="/user/show/88623584-charlotte-p">Charlotte P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88623584-charlotte-p?shelf=grades-4-6">grades-4-6</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88623584-charlotte-p?shelf=best-middle-grade-books">best-middle-grade-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2576697481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17254856938877953978">I usually find winks at other books a bit risky, sometimes presumptuous even. There are two of those winks right at the beginning of the Archibald Finch adventure, one to Harry Potter and one to The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe. But they're different than what I've seen too many times before. They work, because they're more like an homage, a way for the author to pay all due respect, before moving beyond the expected.<br/>Unlike other books, the goal is definitely not to copy something, or to mak</span>
  <span id="freeText17254856938877953978" style="display:none">I usually find winks at other books a bit risky, sometimes presumptuous even. There are two of those winks right at the beginning of the Archibald Finch adventure, one to Harry Potter and one to The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe. But they're different than what I've seen too many times before. They work, because they're more like an homage, a way for the author to pay all due respect, before moving beyond the expected.<br />Unlike other books, the goal is definitely not to copy something, or to make fun of that something. It's more to say: I could go that way, but I won't. I think the author could do that since he knew this story would stand out as totally unique and quite revolutionary. It's clear that he knew where the story was going, what the point was in the end. I see the winks as a way to set the record straight and to indicate what's to come, by saying: this is different. And different it sure is. Most middle grade and teen fiction books are essentially built on the same assumptions, the same legends, the same myths and as a whole, on the same references that honestly we all have in mind when starting such books.<br />Here all those references and many pre-conceived ideas get shattered one after another, from the caricatural idea we have of witches to the very concept of magic, where it comes from, what it's made of, and the possibility that magic can be based on real stuff, like plants, stones, fish, plus of course some cool runes and inspired incantations.<br />The main myth to be challenged though is the one of dragons and I must say I was getting a little tired of the old usual breed. No matter what how big the nostrils, claws or tails, none were seriously that scary anymore. The dragons in Archibald Finch, on the other hand, those are definitely on the weird and scary side. With bits and pieces of various animals, insects, plants and humans, each creature is more unsettling than the next, only adding to the deep mystery surrounding the story.<br />This book is definitely its own animal. I wish the whole series was already out. So much to take in that I'm getting ready to read it a second time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17254856938877953978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12885980336916240255" style="display:none">Oh my goodness...where to start? This book is amazing. I adore the story, the characters and the writing style! <br />I never read a story like this and it is super fun but it also has powerful moments. Now...what I really want to talk about is the writing style because aaaaaa!!!!! I’m obsessed! It’s unique, it has this quirkiness that’s all its own. <div id="review_2580295744" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2580295744" />
    <a title="Cups and Thoughts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38455298-cups-and-thoughts"><img alt="Cups and Thoughts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573547538p2/38455298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2580295744?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cups and Thoughts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cups and Thoughts" href="/user/show/38455298-cups-and-thoughts">Cups and Thoughts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2580295744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16481910000844895431">This book is just made for the nostalgic, the daydreamers, and the adventurers. There's lots of unique, magical elements going around in the book, while still keeping the family dynamic true to the story. It's amazing to see that family plays a huge part in this book. Most Fantasy novels don't really explore family elements in general , so it's always nice to read about it whenever I get the chance to come across it in a book. The characters are so loveable and charismatic, and the story just su</span>
  <span id="freeText16481910000844895431" style="display:none">This book is just made for the nostalgic, the daydreamers, and the adventurers. There's lots of unique, magical elements going around in the book, while still keeping the family dynamic true to the story. It's amazing to see that family plays a huge part in this book. Most Fantasy novels don't really explore family elements in general , so it's always nice to read about it whenever I get the chance to come across it in a book. The characters are so loveable and charismatic, and the story just sucks you right in! All this talk about antique stores, an old manor, a thousand year old secret, and witches just makes the book brim with so much atmosphere &lt;3 So much Halloween/Autumnal vibes! It's just perfect. October has made me become a major mood reader, and Archibald Finch topped my reading game this month with its immersive story and charming characters. <br /><br />This book switches back and forth between two perspectives - one Hailee who lives in London, and the other of her brother who gets sucked into a world called Lemurea. The transition between both perspectives was done so well! Alongside the magical creatures and wars, we also get to venture around Central London. We get to see a world where witches fight and beasts dwell, but we also get to follow the perspective of a young girl experiencing real life problems. Hailee is lost and upset, but she's also curious and strong. Archibald is brilliant and a tad ignorant, but he's loving and sensitive. Both Hailee and Archibald grow as characters in different ways, which was an absolute delight to see. Although I did enjoy both perspectives, I was definitely more keen to read Hailee's perspective. The setting and antagonist just appealed more to me. Whilst I did enjoy the world of Marodors, Lemurea still remains an unexplored world. It needs more depth and room for the characters to grow and the world to expand. But I know this is only the beginning of Archibald Finch! I can tell that the next book will have lots more in store for us readers! <br /><br />Archibald Finch and The Lost Witches is the perfect fantastical coming of age story. It's action-a=packed, enigmatic, and super charming. I'm not usually one for Middle-grade Fantasy books, but Archibald has my heart&lt;3 I enjoyed every second of it! Please, please pick this book up if you haven't thought of doing so already! <br /><br />Many thanks to Michel Guyon for sending me a copy of the book in exchange for an honest review! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16481910000844895431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3146211008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3146211008" />
    <a title="Judy Parrish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104972795-judy-parrish"><img alt="Judy Parrish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572934541p2/104972795.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3146211008?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judy Parrish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judy Parrish" href="/user/show/104972795-judy-parrish">Judy Parrish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3146211008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7369359980158820952">People don't write books like this anymore. I got entirely lost in this story, and to be honest, I'm not sure I'm completely back yet. I surely left pieces of my heart in Lemurea, with those stranded witches Archibald discovers "down there"......<br/>One thing I found particularly of interest is that the hidden/fantastic world in Archibald Finch is not just scary because of the way it is depicted, or for the frightening descriptions of its monsters; it is also terrifying for everything it implies, in</span>
  <span id="freeText7369359980158820952" style="display:none">People don't write books like this anymore. I got entirely lost in this story, and to be honest, I'm not sure I'm completely back yet. I surely left pieces of my heart in Lemurea, with those stranded witches Archibald discovers "down there"......<br />One thing I found particularly of interest is that the hidden/fantastic world in Archibald Finch is not just scary because of the way it is depicted, or for the frightening descriptions of its monsters; it is also terrifying for everything it implies, in terms of what those young girls had to go through before trading one nightmare for another. As a matter of fact, just thinking so much of this is true or at least based on actual lives, gave me the chills more than once. I really hope this aspect is developed even more in the next books.<br />By the way, by "people don't write books like this anymore", I'm talking about how clever and imaginative this is. Besides Harry Potter, I can't really recall a fantasy novel for middle grade or young adults that carried so much meaning and packed such emotional content, along with the fantasy and magic aspect I mean. I am not saying that fantasy adventure books should always and automatically come with a wagon of deep thoughts, but it's refreshing and reassuring to see that some authors have not given up on the idea.<br />To cap it all, as an added bonus, this book is beautifully written, and the way the text and drawings come together only add to the poetry and old-fashion style of this unique read. I'll say it one more time: People don't write books like this anymore...<br />(For those who've asked me: this is definitely a great read-along book, but perfect for kids interested in reading on their own as well, starting at around 8 and above I would say.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7369359980158820952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2565685394" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2565685394" />
    <a title="Emily Mann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88091893-emily-mann"><img alt="Emily Mann" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2565685394?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily Mann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily Mann" href="/user/show/88091893-emily-mann">Emily Mann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2565685394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9494423320045337977">A newcomer that feels like a classic. There's something about this fantasy tale that reminds me of one of those magical books I read as a kid, that just made me want to read more, and more, and more. You discover the fantastic world of Lemurea through the eyes of Archibald and soon enough, the magic happens, you feel the way he feels, you fear the way he fears, and you doubt the way he doubts. Of course it also has to do with the extraordinary universe he is thrust into, a world that echoes the </span>
  <span id="freeText9494423320045337977" style="display:none">A newcomer that feels like a classic. There's something about this fantasy tale that reminds me of one of those magical books I read as a kid, that just made me want to read more, and more, and more. You discover the fantastic world of Lemurea through the eyes of Archibald and soon enough, the magic happens, you feel the way he feels, you fear the way he fears, and you doubt the way he doubts. Of course it also has to do with the extraordinary universe he is thrust into, a world that echoes the bedtime story his dad told him when he was still safe in his home: "Imagine, waiting for the night to come, the darkest of nights, with no lights but torches, being surrounded by the woods, humongous, deep, impenetrable woods. A world where every shadow gave birth to a new monster. And a new tale." This anecdote/warning echoes through the entire book as a reminder that a mysterious land like Lemurea can be as magical as it can be scary. But for a huge fantasy fan like me, every page evoked that feeling you get when you're warm and cozy under the covers in your bed while it's stormy and dark outside... What an enchanting feeling! What an enchanting book...</span>
  <a data-text-id="9494423320045337977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2651251257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2651251257" />
    <a title="Bekah | Bekah’s Bookshelves Hosford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47517393-bekah-bekah-s-bookshelves-hosford"><img alt="Bekah | Bekah’s Bookshelves Hosford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561899755p2/47517393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2651251257?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bekah | Bekah’s Bookshelves Hosford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bekah | Bekah’s Bookshelves Hosford" href="/user/show/47517393-bekah-bekah-s-bookshelves-hosford">Bekah | Bekah’s Bookshelves Hosford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2651251257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16884213646143821614">In the new fantasy Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches by Michel Guyon, everything frightens curious and precocious Archibald Finch, especially vegetables and his new home, which his family recently inherited from his grandmother.  However, Archibald is willing to face his fears in order to find the Christmas present his parents say they didn't buy him yet. Upon tearing apart the manor and finding an old globe hidden in the library, he, instead of finding his present, has stumbled upon an ancie</span>
  <span id="freeText16884213646143821614" style="display:none">In the new fantasy Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches by Michel Guyon, everything frightens curious and precocious Archibald Finch, especially vegetables and his new home, which his family recently inherited from his grandmother.  However, Archibald is willing to face his fears in order to find the Christmas present his parents say they didn't buy him yet. Upon tearing apart the manor and finding an old globe hidden in the library, he, instead of finding his present, has stumbled upon an ancient family secret. One that he accidentally unlocks and, in a lightning flash and thunder crash, sucks him into another world that definitely does not resemble Narnia.  Archibald must adjust to living in this new frightening land filled with monsters and witches, but is adamant that he will find away to get himself--and his new friends--back home. Meanwhile, back at home, his sister Hailee must come to terms with witnessing Archibald's disappearance and solve the mystery of the globe. As she investigates, trying to find a way to bring her brother back, she discovers she is not the only person interested in the mysteries of the globe, and the other mysterious party is willing to kill in order to obtain it... Michel Guyon seamlessly writes these two parallel stories, alternating each chapter between Archibald's and Hailee's viewpoints, and progressing the story until they intertwine.  As Archibald traverses through a dangerous, new land, seeking answers, Hailee and her new friend must traverse London, also seeking answers while being stalked by danger.  In addition, they both learn not everything is as it seems, to be kind, that determination will see them through, and to have hope that good will triumph. Guyon's frank yet humorous and whimsical writing style mixed with a mysterious, compelling plot make Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches an enchanting read. The illustrations throughout are also gorgeous and full of whimsy,  enhancing the story and adding to the enjoyment of the reader. I also like how he has borrowed from well-known fantasy tropes, such as children being transported to a magical land, but it feels original and all his own. The monsters, which are half monster and half human, really stick out. They are monstrous, but they don't kill. They are created by the evil of the human world and, like evil, can never really die, and there is no cure. Once a monster, always a monster. And yet, Archibald questions this absolute, which I love. I also liked the foreshadowing and hints that lead to some interesting twists and turns. Overall, I loved this book, and I think anyone (but especially those between the ages of 11 and 16) who enjoys fantasy novels embroiled in mystery will devour this novel. I give this book a 5/5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16884213646143821614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2556980690" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2556980690" />
    <a title="Gillian Mescham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87557086-gillian-mescham"><img alt="Gillian Mescham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539925034p2/87557086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2556980690?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gillian Mescham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gillian Mescham" href="/user/show/87557086-gillian-mescham">Gillian Mescham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2556980690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3836131416073530034">I am what you’d call a slow reader. It usually takes me about 10 days to finish a book this size (350 pages). Well… I've read it in two days (and one night). A bit like Archibald, I got sucked into this world the author has created, and in terms of world building, this is truly phenomenal, second only to Harry Potter in my opinion (And I absolutely looove HP).<br/>It’s not so much the concept that is new but rather the content and the very nature of the book, with a really original architecture. Of c</span>
  <span id="freeText3836131416073530034" style="display:none">I am what you’d call a slow reader. It usually takes me about 10 days to finish a book this size (350 pages). Well… I've read it in two days (and one night). A bit like Archibald, I got sucked into this world the author has created, and in terms of world building, this is truly phenomenal, second only to Harry Potter in my opinion (And I absolutely looove HP).<br />It’s not so much the concept that is new but rather the content and the very nature of the book, with a really original architecture. Of course there’s a lot of cool magic and whimsy stuff in this story (from the talking cauldron to the dog-pillow, and those dreamy/nightmarish underworld colonies!) but the real magic resides perhaps in the way the story unfolds, giving a thriller-like rhythm to the book. I just loved travelling from one world to another at each new chapter start, without losing track of the story. Quite the opposite actually since both narratives are not just linked to one another, they also communicate with one another, through clues gathered in both worlds, slowly unveiling the dark secret behind the entire adventure. I think that's one of my "many" favorite things in this book. It is just so ingenious. London on one side. And this dark, mysterious universe on the other, where old myths are debunked and others reinvented. Wait until you meet the “dragons” made in Lemurea, that’s one magic twist on something I thought was pretty much frozen and established as a legend by now! But this dust-off is so refreshing and just plain exciting.<br />The book also debunks quite a few clichés about witches, and I love the way the historic context is put in perspective as a background compass. Again, the merging between our world and Middle Age drama flows flawlessly, that’s probably why I couldn’t let go of the book, and finished it so quickly. The humor throughout the story and dialogues surely helped as well.<br />Overall, Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches is an addicting read, full of surprises. I can’t wait for the next book in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3836131416073530034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2550034320" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2550034320" />
    <a title="Greg Lamb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87557674-greg-lamb"><img alt="Greg Lamb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567622766p2/87557674.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2550034320?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg Lamb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg Lamb" href="/user/show/87557674-greg-lamb">Greg Lamb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2550034320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer746783831350074095">This could have been the story of a fairly regular, wimpy, lonely boy who loses his weird grandma, moves into her manor with his parents and discovers an antique globe that will seal his fate, transporting him into some mysterious land haunted by some weird breed of monsters. It could have been that. But it wouldn't have been that original or interesting. So thank God it's not that. Not just that I should say.<br/>Where Archibald goes and whom he meets down there, that's what's original, that's what'</span>
  <span id="freeText746783831350074095" style="display:none">This could have been the story of a fairly regular, wimpy, lonely boy who loses his weird grandma, moves into her manor with his parents and discovers an antique globe that will seal his fate, transporting him into some mysterious land haunted by some weird breed of monsters. It could have been that. But it wouldn't have been that original or interesting. So thank God it's not that. Not just that I should say.<br />Where Archibald goes and whom he meets down there, that's what's original, that's what's really fascinating. And I weigh my words carefully. I actually think this book is pure genius.<br />First the writing is superb. Reminds me of that amazing teacher I had in 8th Grade who had that unique way of telling stories, by picking the right words, weird words often, but somehow weaved into something intriguing and just pure sugar to me. This is all the more brilliant that the author is French I believe! And the humor is pretty goddam good as well. I cracked up more than once, even though the whole concept is really dark. Here we get to the original part, point blank: witch-hunting in the Middle Ages! Here's one thing I never quite expected to find in a children/YA book. Ever. But it makes so much sense and becomes so relevant as the story develops. Archibald shows the way of course, but he is not the story, not really, he is just the guide. The story revolves around those poor young girls, and what's happened since that fateful, dramatic and messed up tragedy of an event, 500 years ago.<br />I know this is the beginning of a series, and I'm loving the idea. But what I can't wait to read is the prequel. Again, genius stuff.</span>
  <a data-text-id="746783831350074095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2566529297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2566529297" />
    <a title="Kaitlyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88210862-kaitlyn"><img alt="Kaitlyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539918110p2/88210862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2566529297?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlyn" href="/user/show/88210862-kaitlyn">Kaitlyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2566529297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8455211540509492434">I started reading this book without knowing that much of what I was about to discover was real... or at least based on true events. It was a bit of a shock, in a good way. I was kind of like Archibald, who thinks at first that he must be dreaming, only to realize that Lemurea is real, so that he'd better adapt to this crazy underworld quickly if he wants to survive. And survive is definitely the right word, because Lemurea is not really the place you'd want to fall into if you had a choice. It's</span>
  <span id="freeText8455211540509492434" style="display:none">I started reading this book without knowing that much of what I was about to discover was real... or at least based on true events. It was a bit of a shock, in a good way. I was kind of like Archibald, who thinks at first that he must be dreaming, only to realize that Lemurea is real, so that he'd better adapt to this crazy underworld quickly if he wants to survive. And survive is definitely the right word, because Lemurea is not really the place you'd want to fall into if you had a choice. It's dark, it's eerie and it's infested with those more than peculiar beasts, Marodors as they're called, part human, part animals, parts... unknown(!)... unless you land in one of those colonies dotting that dark world. Those are really really cool, and I'd sign up anytime for a summer camp in one of them! They are a bit like beacons, of light, of hope... and most of all, magic, with waves of northern lights rising from monumental stones also used as shields against those Marodors. That's where the book gets really outstanding, by conveying and emphasizing every bit of contrast between the beauty and (relative) peace in those colonies, and the chaos around, between the naiveté of the young witches' life, and the freak-show waiting outside, or knocking at the door actually...<br />This is akin to the fantasy worlds I have become addicted to, from Hogwarts to Narnia and the Shire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8455211540509492434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10661883284588689324">I think I read a girl say in her Goodreads review that she wanted to be Faerydae. And I get it, Faerydae is quite a tough girl and could be quite a role model for many. But me personally, I'd want to be Maven. Not really surprising when you know I've identified with Hermione for the last 18 years... Maven's the golem nerd, the magic stones nerd if you prefer. And since everything, or most things at least, revolve around golems in this crazy scary world of Lemurea, then Maven ends up being at the</span>
  <span id="freeText10661883284588689324" style="display:none">I think I read a girl say in her Goodreads review that she wanted to be Faerydae. And I get it, Faerydae is quite a tough girl and could be quite a role model for many. But me personally, I'd want to be Maven. Not really surprising when you know I've identified with Hermione for the last 18 years... Maven's the golem nerd, the magic stones nerd if you prefer. And since everything, or most things at least, revolve around golems in this crazy scary world of Lemurea, then Maven ends up being at the center of the story, and at the center of every battle against the Marodors, those mysterious creatures that besiege Maven and her friends in their colonies built throughout Lemurea. And Maven is so funny too, it doesn't hurt. Some of her dialogues with Archibald in particular are hilarious, much like a lot of the humor in the whole book actually.<br />There are a lot things I adored in this book. The premise and the eerie vibe of the manor at the beginning, the science and herbology behind the young witches' survival story, etc, etc. But my favorite is really the witches themselves and what they represent, in terms of balance between tough, cute, weird enough, smart, sensitive, funny with a dark side. Me, me, me, me, me, me, me, or at least that's what I aim towards. I mean, who doesn't want to be all that!?!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2945344131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4297597411244453975">I'm addicted to checking out other people's reviews. I can't help it. I'm often disappointed but I must say, for once, I agree with essentially everything that has been said so far about this book: Truly original premise, fantastic world-building, incredible character development with really interesting characters, old myths revisited and completely reinvented, and that new take on dragons (my favorite part I think)... This is an incredible, well-crafted, surprisingly complex story (for middle g</span>
  <span id="freeText4297597411244453975" style="display:none">I'm addicted to checking out other people's reviews. I can't help it. I'm often disappointed but I must say, for once, I agree with essentially everything that has been said so far about this book: Truly original premise, fantastic world-building, incredible character development with really interesting characters, old myths revisited and completely reinvented, and that new take on dragons (my favorite part I think)... This is an incredible, well-crafted, surprisingly complex story (for middle grade I mean).<br />Past the discovery chapter and the introduction to a new fantasy world, the story feels so big suddenly, as if there was something bigger behind it. And that feeling follows you through the entire book.<br />I love fairytales and I would probably manage to live off fairy dust (or moonlight, like Luna in the Girl who Drank the Moon). But this is not just about magic. There's about this story that also feels so real. The witch-hunting aspect of it really resonated with me, profoundly.<br />One of the best books I have read this year, and in a long time for that matter. A big book in so many ways, with a big potential for the whole series to come. I highly recommend.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10319710014260052719">Who are those young girls Archibald finds in Lemurea?   <span id="freeText10319710014260052719" style="display:none">Who are those young girls Archibald finds in Lemurea? The answer is more than surprising, like so many elements of this story...<br />What exactly are those monsters haunting the woods, skies and rivers of that mysterious underworld Archibald got thrown into? The answer to this one is even more unexpected...<br />I'm rarely rarely surprised by books, especially middle-grade these days... but this one really got to my heart and soul. Behind and beyond the often funny lines and dialogues, which are very enjoyable, this is such a deep, inspired story. Just knowing there's more of this story to come makes me excited, especially since there's so much mystery left to unveil.<br />I loved this book on my own, now I'm about to start reading it again, aloud this time, with my kids. A dead grandmother.<br/><br/>Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches is an exciting adventure between two worlds, two siblings, and a rich cast of secondary characters. Archibald finds himself lost in a strange land full of terrible monsters and young girls who claim to be witches.   <span id="freeText7749818085695065488" style="display:none">A strange boy. A feisty sister. An old globe. A dead grandmother.<br /><br />Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches is an exciting adventure between two worlds, two siblings, and a rich cast of secondary characters. Archibald finds himself lost in a strange land full of terrible monsters and young girls who claim to be witches. His sister, Hailee, is left behind with the mystery of Archibald’s disappearance and a sinister man trying to steal her only clue.<br /><br />I loved every minute of this book. The illustrations are rich and scary, the plot is faced paced and well spun, and the writing is witty and thought provoking. <br /><br />I highly recommend this book! It was the perfect way for me to end 2018.</span>

<div id="review_2964113058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2964113058" />
    <a title="Iris H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102244339-iris-h"><img alt="Iris H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567755450p2/102244339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2964113058?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iris H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iris H." href="/user/show/102244339-iris-h">Iris H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2964113058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9323762980966940166">Just a few days ago, I wrote a quick review on this very platform, explaining how I feel about key chapters/scenes that come to define an entire book, if not a whole genre, fantasy in this case.<br/>That particular review was about a classic of children literature, "The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe", and the chapter/scene relevant to my point was what I like to call the "Narnia landing", with the magical setting including just a few elements: the snow, the forrest, a few fur coats, and a lonely l</span>
  <span id="freeText9323762980966940166" style="display:none">Just a few days ago, I wrote a quick review on this very platform, explaining how I feel about key chapters/scenes that come to define an entire book, if not a whole genre, fantasy in this case.<br />That particular review was about a classic of children literature, "The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe", and the chapter/scene relevant to my point was what I like to call the "Narnia landing", with the magical setting including just a few elements: the snow, the forrest, a few fur coats, and a lonely lamppost... To me, fantasy at its finest.<br />I just happened to come upon another one of those magical scenes, which I have now dreamed of for the past two nights. Without going too much into details, since I wouldn't want to ruin the moment for others, it basically takes place when Archibald, the boy at the center of this story, lands in the fantastic world of Lemurea, along with half his bedroom. (Again, I will let you find out how he got himself into this predicament, and the kind of adventure that awaits him, with the most extraordinary creatures I've ever read about, and an amazingly well-crafted narrative.)<br />Unlike the Narnia adventures, no movie has been made of Archibald Finch (just yet), but a formidable double page illustration in the book helps translate the magic of that scene beautifully.<br />There are many enchanting and thrilling things in this book, and many fabulous illustrations opening each chapter and scattered in between. In fact, the story only gets better from that point on. But... none other than the "landing" scene gave me such pleasure and inspiration. This is a rather rare occurrence for me. It's that tingling you get when discovering a new fantasy world, a world you know will have a huge impact on you and the way you perceive fantasy.<br />Most of us middle grade fans would love to go through a wardrobe and roll into the snow by that lamppost, and we are all secretly, or openly, waiting for that admission letter from Hogwarts. Now, after reading this book, I think the next time I go to my parents' home, I might go through the attic looking for the sort of old relic Archibald found in his grandma's manor, and see where it leads me. I might "land" in the same dark woods of Lemurea... In the meantime, I'll keep dreaming about it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9323762980966940166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Then later on I told her I really really want to read it. Obviously, she had read the book till then. She told me she will let me borrow it to read.   <span id="freeText14234600492464058485" style="display:none">When my bookish best friend received the review copy of this book, I was instantly obsessed with it. Then later on I told her I really really want to read it. Obviously, she had read the book till then. She told me she will let me borrow it to read. FINALLY, I got the book from her recently and I was just so so happy. I was so excited to start reading it. <br /><br />FLASH forward to Today! I finished the book Omg!<br /><br />Michael Guyon wrote a master piece, literally. I mean where should I begin? This book was everything and more. You know the best part? The illustrations killed it like Woah! <br />There was magic, the connection of history with fiction, a teleportation device to travel to an elseworld and so much more. <br />Don't even get me started on the characters, world building and plot twist. This book gives the best message to both children and adults alike. Learning is a never ending process. You can make the impossible happen and that you are all smart in your own ways. This book literally boosted my confidence. <br /><br />Thank you, thank you Michael for writing such an extra ordinary book which made me laugh, took me on an amazing adventure and introducing me to those horrifying morouders who can actually be saved. <br />I can't wait for the second Book. You guys, please go get this book and read. You will love it so much. </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88423870-erin-allen?shelf=must-read-for-kids">must-read-for-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88423870-erin-allen?shelf=grades-4-6">grades-4-6</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88423870-erin-allen?shelf=best-kids-books">best-kids-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88423870-erin-allen?shelf=best-fantasy-kids-books">best-fantasy-kids-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2572790898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer676531483584788050">Maybe it's because I'm fixated on books turned into movies and/or movies turned books, but the whole time I was reading this book, I said to myself: I can't wait to see the movie!<br/>I don't think it's only due to my obsession though. I would credit that to the absolutely gorgeous illustrations, which help create a storyboard feel and also connect each story with each other. Yes there are two stories, which makes me think that this could have easily been two books, but it's so much more fun to read </span>
  <span id="freeText676531483584788050" style="display:none">Maybe it's because I'm fixated on books turned into movies and/or movies turned books, but the whole time I was reading this book, I said to myself: I can't wait to see the movie!<br />I don't think it's only due to my obsession though. I would credit that to the absolutely gorgeous illustrations, which help create a storyboard feel and also connect each story with each other. Yes there are two stories, which makes me think that this could have easily been two books, but it's so much more fun to read both at the same time, each sharing half of the chapters. And it's sublimely executed too, probably because the stories have so much to do with one another, kind of like in a Tarantino movie where lots of things happen and it all comes together and makes sense in the end.<br />And here I go again with the movie thing. But I'm serious, this has movie written all over it. In fact, I just realized, in many ways, it's written very much like a screenplay.<br />The sounds, the images, the flashes, the smells, it's all in there. That's why it felt so easy and natural to get on board with the story and get transported into this new world. It felt real. And since on of everything the story IS real, the back story about witch-hunting I mean, it all works out. Oh and the present tense, hellooo!! Just like most screenplays! If that doesn't rhyme with movie, then I'm really obsessed and crazy. I'd be curious to know if the author did all this intentionally. Now I need to know or it's going to make me really crazy!<br />I know I'm right. Lol. Can't wait to see the movie.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18080227575839512950">Didn't expect much, except another book about magic and fantasy trying to copy Harry Potter... so I was definitely surprised.<br/>I won't say that this is better than Harry Potter, nothing is. Besides, I've got to see what comes next, in book 2, 3 and however many there will be.   <span id="freeText18080227575839512950" style="display:none">Didn't expect much, except another book about magic and fantasy trying to copy Harry Potter... so I was definitely surprised.<br />I won't say that this is better than Harry Potter, nothing is. Besides, I've got to see what comes next, in book 2, 3 and however many there will be. But let's just say they is a incredible start.<br />The writing is so fun, the story so deep and addictive, and the characters so moving. I have not felt this way since, okay fine you guessed it, yes, Harry Potter.<br />I really like the darkness surrounding the whole adventure and when I found out that a lot of the back story is actually true, I actually got the chills. It's not really a scary read though because there's a ton a humor in the writing and the style that brings things back down to a lighter mood right at the right time.<br />The deeper I was getting into the story, the more I kept thinking of movies and director for some reason. Of course the first Harry Potter, but there's also some Tim Burton spirit and vibe in this drama. And even some Tarantino I think, the way things come together little by little from multiple different stories that meet and make sense in the end. This is really grand. Archibald Finch is my new best friend!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18080227575839512950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2596855778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8755707766355601966">I saw an ad for this book somewhere online that said: Caution, may contain magic. And I think it totally sums up the book. A magical journey, with a ton a really good humor.<br/>The magic in Archibald Finch is truly amazing, but the way I see it, it's not really because of the actual magic inside (the secret underworld, the fantastic creatures, the witches' weapons, etc.) but more because of the incredible atmosphere (so mysterious and eerie), that shrouds the story. Or should I say the stories, sinc</span>
  <span id="freeText8755707766355601966" style="display:none">I saw an ad for this book somewhere online that said: Caution, may contain magic. And I think it totally sums up the book. A magical journey, with a ton a really good humor.<br />The magic in Archibald Finch is truly amazing, but the way I see it, it's not really because of the actual magic inside (the secret underworld, the fantastic creatures, the witches' weapons, etc.) but more because of the incredible atmosphere (so mysterious and eerie), that shrouds the story. Or should I say the stories, since there are actually two distinct stories, which even though they are unfolding in different worlds (our almost normal world of 2018, and a definitely less normal world of way back then, in the Dark Ages...)<br />About half of the chapters take place in one world. And the other half in the other. And just for the record, there's no better half. What's actually interesting is that at first you wonder which world you prefer (For me it was Lemurea), until you realize (around chapter 6) how intertwined those two worlds are, and how they co-exist and work together to help us make sense of things. It all ends up reading as one story. And that might be the most magical thing of all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8755707766355601966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4447076522379187429" style="display:none">I love everything Da Vinci so even though LDV is only part of the backstory here, I really enjoyed all the references to the great Renaissance Man. Seeing the tank that LDV imagined come to life and be put to use, was truly a great surprise, especially against the most unexpected enemy! I had seen prior attempts at using LDV's work in some novels, but never in a book for middle grade or young adult audience. And this is done in such imaginative way that it actually works, and would almost make you feel that LDV indeed created that invention for the purpose of fighting Marodors in Lemurea..! Who would have thought?!? What I also found fascinating in the book is the implied connection between Da Vinci and the world of witches. That is something I really wish the author will explore further in the following books in the series.</span>
