So I decided to grab Archibald again a couple days ago and read it from a to z.<br/>There were so many things I didn't notice the first time, especially in the intricate ways the characters are connected, or the way they become linked to one another little by little.   <span id="freeText10126369408936702806" style="display:none">I had read this book during Christmas time and really enjoyed it, but we had a lot of family over back then so I couldn't quite focus on the story as much as I wished. It took me a week to read, with many interruptions. So I decided to grab Archibald again a couple days ago and read it from a to z.<br />There were so many things I didn't notice the first time, especially in the intricate ways the characters are connected, or the way they become linked to one another little by little. It's that aspect that moved me in particular. Archibald Finch is as much a book about fantasy, monsters, parallel worlds, relics, magic and witches, as it is about friendship, family and what it means to rely on each other.<br />I found the book very entertaining in December. Now I find it highly inspiring as well.</span>

<div id="review_3148404709" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3148404709" />
    <a title="Kaitlyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97845709-kaitlyn"><img alt="Kaitlyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603931399p2/97845709.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2542296362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2542296362" />
    <a title="Alisa Ellie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66699689-alisa-ellie"><img alt="Alisa Ellie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535663545p2/66699689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2542296362?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alisa Ellie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alisa Ellie" href="/user/show/66699689-alisa-ellie">Alisa Ellie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2542296362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8170592291271713099"><blockquote>
  <b>“Mankind has repeated the same mistakes, over and over, for centuries now, never learning from them. I have come to believe that people don’t <i>want</i> to change their ways. Therefore, they don’t deserve to be saved.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches is a story that I'd rather prefer to read or to listen to when I was a kid. However, I took my pleasure to get acquainted with it now as an adult. It felt like a perfect bedtime tale, not the kind of a scary one despite the monstrous developments,</span>
  <span id="freeText8170592291271713099" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“Mankind has repeated the same mistakes, over and over, for centuries now, never learning from them. I have come to believe that people don’t <i>want</i> to change their ways. Therefore, they don’t deserve to be saved.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Archibald Finch and the Lost Witches is a story that I'd rather prefer to read or to listen to when I was a kid. However, I took my pleasure to get acquainted with it now as an adult. It felt like a perfect bedtime tale, not the kind of a scary one despite the monstrous developments, but a story that educates and enlightens whilst telling a great adventure. The world-building is engrossing and mastered with great fantasy. I was caught off guard with some dialogues that I couldn’t stop laughing at so it’s funny and witty as well.<br /><br />I like how the author positions the girls in this story, young witches with great courage and wisdom. They were saved from the horrors and savagery of the world during the witch-hunting times and were transferred to another dimension where they turned into warriors from unable to protect themselves, little girls. A perfect representation of independent women who can rule the world with the strength not inferior to men.<br /><br />The author skillfully put the analogy into these two worlds - the real one from which our protagonist Archibald was whisked through a magic globe, and the underworld of Lemurea inhabited with young witches fighting monsters. This new make-believe world can be easily used as exaggerate matrix of good and evil though not without a vital message hidden in the analogy. I was pleased with the way Archibald changed the witches’ perception of monsters those were hunted and caged for a long time. Finally, the monsters turned out to be not what they were expected. Even in a damaged and damned creature can be found a spark of hope and aspiration for good. And of course, this book is not without the ambition for world peace, equality and the good to defeat evil, as all kind stories are.<br /><br />As you see, the story has much to tell and teach a young mind who lives in such a confusing world as ours. It definitely gets my recommendation and deserves a place in a family library. Can’t wait to have my kids to read this book to them.<br /><br /><b>[I guess I will put it on one shelf with Harry Potter books. That means something, huh?]</b><br /><br /><i>**The book was gifted by the author in exchange for my honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8170592291271713099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AZ+jV6bflI+dXuo1d7m3jhF+NIXIo3UbA1XpMGyXKvY7ucqFHYFd5zp1XlSATL1RxyHTTQYu+3xYK6+BodTYbA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12947276149837079812">The author was born in France, in a small medieval town perched on a rock, surrounded by high walls, with the remains of an ancient fortress at its heart. That’s where he got his first brush with old myths, puzzling legends and dark Middle Age tales.<br/>While his childhood fed his fertile imagination, his travels as a reporter, from Bosnia all the way to Afghanistan, were crucial in shaping his view o</span>
  <span id="freeText12947276149837079812" style="display:none">The author was born in France, in a small medieval town perched on a rock, surrounded by high walls, with the remains of an ancient fortress at its heart. That’s where he got his first brush with old myths, puzzling legends and dark Middle Age tales.<br />While his childhood fed his fertile imagination, his travels as a reporter, from Bosnia all the way to Afghanistan, were crucial in shaping his view of the world.<br />Not unlike Archibald’s sister in the book, Michel has indeed learned a thing or two about mining for clues and connecting the dots. For 10 years, he was an investigative journalist for newspapers in magazines and Europe. He also published several books for children and young adults —not to mention his communication work for the European Space Agency, where he was tasked to make space exploration less opaque to the public.<br />Writing this latest adventure has been a fun endeavor for Michel. Like most of the author’s work though, there’s more than meets the eye. A fervent advocate of learning via entertainment, he always strives to shed light on important subject matters —in this case, Women’s rights, wars, and the future of our planet. That logic was key to the making of Archibald Finch, a magic potion mixing science with science fiction, fantasy with actual events, and fictional heroes with historic characters. Giving life to the most fantastic beasts and the most captivating story was indeed an opportunity to dig deep into the roots of witch-hunting, and explore one of the darkest episodes of Human History —of course with the right dose of humor and fun.<br />Today, Michel spends his life between Los Angeles and New York, where he also works as a photographer, mainly for the Movie industry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12947276149837079812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
